If there are many streams\n715:   // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n716:   if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n717:     return;\n718:   }\n719: \n720:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n721:     return;\n722:   }\n723: \n724:   const uint64_t limit =\n725:       runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n726: \n727:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n728:     // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n729:     // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n730:     // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n731:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n732:       return;\n733:     }\n734:   } else {\n735:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n736:       return;\n737:     }\n738:   }\n739: \n740:   if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n741:     stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n742: \n743:     // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n744:     drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n745: \n746:     doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n747:                       \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n748:   }\n749: }\n750: \n751: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onGoAway(GoAwayErrorCode) {\n752:   // Currently we do nothing with remote go away frames. void ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::maybeRecordLastByteReceived(bool end_stream) {\n1303:   // If recreateStream is called, the HCM rewinds state and may send more encodeData calls.\n1304:   if connection_manager_.dispatcher_->timeSource());\n1307:     ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(debug, \"request end stream timestamp recorded\", *this);\n1308:   }\n1309: }\n1310: \n1311: // Ordering in this function is complicated, but important.\n1312: //\n1313: // We want to do minimal work before selecting route and creating a filter\n1314: // chain to maximize the number of requests which get custom filter behavior,\n1315: // e.g. registering access logging.\n1316: //\n1317: // This must be balanced by doing sanity checking for invalid requests (one\n1318: // can't route select properly without full headers), checking state required to\n1319: // serve error responses (connection close, head requests, etc), and\n1320: // modifications which may themselves affect route selection.\n1321: void \\n259: void ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream(ActiveStream& stream, bool check_for_deferred_close) {\\n260:   // The order of what happens in this routine is important and a little complicated. We first see\\n261:   // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\\n262:   // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\\n263:   // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01MQAYSEbodWn229XrdFWhms","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01RdxB4Z9DKFGydrnKWi7GVj","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Envoy HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is critical infrastructure for HTTP protocol handling, stream lifecycle management, and filter chain execution. Analysis of `conn_manager_impl.cc`, `filter_manager.cc`, and `header_map_impl.cc` reveals **5 significant untested code paths** that could allow bugs in connection management, error handling, metadata processing, and filter state transitions to slip through. These gaps primarily affect error scenarios, edge cases in filter iteration, and complex state transitions that are difficult to trigger in normal operation.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Codec Error Handling Under Connection State Changes\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~463-482 (handleCodecErrorImpl, handleCodecError, handleCodecOverloadError)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Description**:\nThe functions `handleCodecError()`, `handleCodecErrorImpl()`, and `handleCodecOverloadError()` are responsible for terminating the connection when the codec encounters protocol errors or overload conditions. These functions are called from `onData()` after codec dispatch fails. However, the test suite lacks comprehensive coverage for:\n- Codec errors that occur when there are **active streams with various states** (some completed, some in-progress, some in filter chain)\n- The interaction between `handleCodecError()` and deferred deletion of streams\n- Proper cleanup when codec errors occur during H/1 vs H/2 vs H/3 protocols\n- The `handleCodecOverloadError()` path which sets `OverloadManager` response flag instead of protocol error flag\n\n**Proposed Test**: `CodecErrorWithActiveStreamsInFilterChain`\n- Create multiple concurrent streams in different states:\n  - Stream 1: stuck in decoder filter (StopAllIteration)\n  - Stream 2: waiting for upstream response\n  - Stream 3: about to encode response\n- Inject a codec error via mock codec\n- Verify:\n  - All active streams are reset with proper response flags\n  - Response flag is set correctly (DownstreamProtocolError vs OverloadManager)\n  - Connection is properly closed without leaks\n  - Stream details in logs reflect the error state\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nCodec errors are rare but catastrophic. If stream cleanup is incorrect, it could lead to:\n- Resource leaks (streams not deleted from streams_ list)\n- Incorrect stats increments (double-counting, missing counters)\n- Filters accessing invalid stream state after closure\n- Clients not receiving reset notifications\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Connection Drain Sequence Edge Cases\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~756-794 (onIdleTimeout, onConnectionDurationTimeout, onDrainTimeout, startDrainSequence)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Description**:\nThe drain sequence is initiated when timeouts occur or when connection should enter graceful shutdown. The code paths handle:\n- Idle timeout with active streams → start drain\n- Max connection duration reached with/without HTTP/1 safe mode\n- Drain timeout transition from NotDraining → Closing\n\nHowever, tests do not cover:\n- **Drain sequence when connection has NO streams** (idle_timeout fires but streams_ is empty) → should immediately close\n- **Simultaneous timeout signals** (both idle_timeout and connection_duration_timer_ fire in quick succession)\n- **HTTP/1 soft drain** path where `soft_drain_http1_` is set and `codec_->goAway()` must not be called\n- **Drain state transitions** when streams finish during drain sequence\n- **checkForDeferredClose() interaction** with drain timeouts\n\n**Proposed Test**: `DrainSequenceWithNoStreamsAndQuickTimer`\n- Setup connection with idle_timeout and max_connection_duration both very short (10ms)\n- Do NOT create any streams\n- Wait for first timeout to fire\n- Verify:\n  - First timeout initiates drain correctly\n  - Stream list is empty, so connection closes immediately\n  - Second timeout does not cause double-close or state corruption\n  - Stats show proper transition (idle_timeout incremented, then close stats)\n  - For HTTP/1, soft drain flag is set correctly and codec doesn't receive goAway()\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nDrain logic is complex with multiple interlocking conditions. Bugs here could cause:\n- Graceful shutdowns to become abrupt (incomplete drains)\n- Connections to hang (drain never completes)\n- Double-close attempts (crashes or assertion failures)\n- Resource leaks in drain timer management\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Request Header Validation with Redirect and Transform Actions\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1200-1250 (validateHeaders path with header validation, transformation, redirect)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateHeaders()` function validates and transforms request headers. It handles multiple response codes:\n- HTTP 400 (BadRequest) for most failures\n- HTTP 501 (NotImplemented) for InvalidTransferEncoding\n- HTTP 307 (TemporaryRedirect) for path normalization redirects\n\nHowever, test coverage gaps include:\n- **Redirect responses with Location header** when `redirect=true && !is_grpc`\n- **GRPC-specific validation** failures (grpc_status set to Internal instead of response code)\n- **validateTrailers()** function (~1256-1300) which has similar structure but handles trailers validation with different codec-specific behavior for H/2 vs H/1 vs H/3\n- **Interaction with early_header_mutations** during validation failure\n- **ResponseCodeDetails tracking** when validation fails (must be set before sendLocalReply)\n\n**Proposed Test**: `RequestHeaderValidationWithRedirectAndGRPC`\n- Test case 1 (non-GRPC redirect):\n  - Send request with invalid path requiring normalization (e.g., double slashes)\n  - Verify: 307 response with Location header set to normalized path\n  - Stats show `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_` incremented\n  - ResponseCodeDetails set before response sent\n\n- Test case 2 (GRPC validation failure):\n  - Send GRPC request with invalid header underscore (H/2 protocol)\n  - Verify: Stream reset (not 400) per H/2 codec behavior\n  - ResponseCodeDetails set to appropriate UHV code\n  - Stats show `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_`\n\n- Test case 3 (trailers validation for H/1):\n  - Send HTTP/1 request with trailers\n  - Trailers contain invalid underscore in header name\n  - Verify: 400 BadRequest sent (not reset) per H/1 codec behavior\n  - Differs from H/2 reset behavior\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nHeader validation is first-line security. Bugs could cause:\n- Unsafe requests to bypass validation and reach upstream\n- Incorrect redirect responses leading to client loops\n- GRPC validation failures going undetected\n- Path traversal or injection attacks not blocked\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Filter Chain Iteration with Mixed Watermark States\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1625-1633 (handleDataIfStopAll), ~800-878 (decodeTrailers/encodeTrailers), ~880-933 (decodeMetadata)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe filter iteration logic handles three states for each filter:\n- `CanContinue` (no stop)\n- `StopSingleIteration` (stop this frame only, continue others)\n- `StopAllIteration` / `StopAllWatermark` (stop all frames until filter explicitly continues)\n\nThe code must handle:\n- Trailers added during data frames when filters have stopped\n- Metadata arriving after headers when chain is partially aborted\n- **Data arrival when filter is in StopAllWatermark state** → `handleDataIfStopAll()` must buffer data without continuing iteration\n- **Trailers during StopAllWatermark** → special handling in `decodeTrailers()` to skip stopped filters\n- **Metadata when decoder_filter_chain_aborted_** → must be saved and not discarded\n\nTests do not cover:\n- Trailers added by a filter while **previous filter is in StopAllWatermark state**\n- Metadata flowing through when **decoder_filter_chain_aborted_ is true** but filters haven't formally stopped\n- **Multiple metadata maps** arriving in sequence when chain is partially stopped\n- **Data + Trailers + Metadata order permutations** with StopAllWatermark filters\n\n**Proposed Test**: `FilterIterationTrailersWithStopAllWatermarkAndMetadata`\n- Setup 3 filters: F1 (decoder), F2 (decoder), F3 (terminal)\n- F1.decodeHeaders() → returns StopAllWatermark\n- Test harness calls F1.continueDecoding() with data and trailers together\n- Meanwhile F3 has generated and queued metadata for injection\n- Verify:\n  - F1 continues with both data and trailers\n  - Trailers properly delivered to F2 and F3\n  - Metadata queued during trailers processing is properly buffered\n  - No double-iteration of filters\n  - `iterate_from_current_filter_` flag correctly set to restart from F1\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nFilter state machine is complex and order-dependent. Bugs could cause:\n- Filters receiving data/trailers twice\n- Filters skipped entirely (data flows around them)\n- Deadlocks (filter waits for continuation that never comes)\n- Memory exhaustion (metadata/trailers stored but never processed)\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Recreation During Response Encoding with Complex State\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2461-2487 (recreateStream function with state transitions)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe `recreateStream()` function is called in rare cases (e.g., cache filter inject) to restart request processing on same connection. It:\n1. Sets `state_.is_internally_destroyed_ = true`\n2. Calls `doEndStream()` which resets the stream\n3. Creates a new stream and passes it back\n\nThis path is complex because:\n- The original stream's response_encoder is nulled to prevent double-reset notification\n- Deferred close check is disabled during recreation to allow new stream creation\n- Filter manager state must be properly reset between old and new stream\n- Response body encoding stops and switches to new stream context\n\nTest coverage gaps:\n- **Recreation when filters are in various stopped states** (StopAllIteration, etc.)\n- **Recreation with buffered trailers** from the original request\n- **Recreation with half-closed streams** (client sent end_stream, upstream hasn't)\n- **Stats and logging** around recreation (do stats reflect one stream or two?)\n- **Connection-level state** preservation (drain state, active stream list updates)\n- **Timeout state** - are stream timers properly cleaned up?\n\n**Proposed Test**: `RecreateStreamDuringFilterIterationWithTrailers`\n- Setup stream with request headers and trailers\n- Send headers → F1.decodeHeaders() returns StopAllIteration\n- Cache filter calls `encodeHeaders()` with modified request\n- Recreation triggered via `recreateStream()`\n- Verify:\n  - Original stream properly destroyed (state_.is_internally_destroyed_ = true)\n  - New stream created with same response_encoder\n  - Trailers from original request are not duplicated in new stream\n  - Filter timers (request_header_timer_, stream_idle_timeout) are reset\n  - Stream ID in stats reflects new stream, not old one\n  - `checkForDeferredClose()` is NOT called during recreation\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nRecreation is an internal implementation detail used by advanced filters. Bugs could cause:\n- Resource leaks (old stream never fully cleaned up)\n- Duplicate trailers/metadata in new stream\n- Timing attacks (old timers firing after new stream created)\n- Client confusion (stream reset notification + new response from same stream ID)\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\nThe analysis focused on:\n\n- **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc** - Connection lifecycle, codec management, stream creation, timeout handling, drain sequences\n- **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h** - Public interfaces and state machine definitions\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.cc** - Tertiary test file\n- **test/common/http/filter_manager_test.cc** - Filter manager unit tests\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h/cc** - Test infrastructure and mocks\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations for Test Implementation\n\n1. **Prioritize Gap 1 and Gap 2** (HIGH risk): These affect core connection/stream lifecycle\n2. **Use existing test infrastructure** in `conn_manager_impl_test_base.h` for mocks and setup\n3. **Leverage InSequence** for strict ordering verification of codec/stream operations\n4. **Create reusable test fixtures** for common scenarios (N streams in various states, timeout sequences)\n5. **Add mutation testing** to catch subtle state bugs (e.g., forgot to set response_flag)\n6. **Monitor stats assertions** - The code paths handle:\n- Idle timeout with active streams → start drain\n- Max connection duration reached with/without HTTP/1 safe mode\n- Drain timeout transition from NotDraining → Closing\n\nHowever, tests do not cover:\n- **Drain sequence when connection has NO streams** (idle_timeout fires but streams_ is empty) → should immediately close\n- **Simultaneous timeout signals** (both idle_timeout and connection_duration_timer_ fire in quick succession)\n- **HTTP/1 soft drain** path where `soft_drain_http1_` is set and `codec_->goAway()` must not be called\n- **Drain state transitions** when streams finish during drain sequence\n- **checkForDeferredClose() interaction** with drain timeouts\n\n**Proposed Test**: `DrainSequenceWithNoStreamsAndQuickTimer`\n- Setup connection with idle_timeout and max_connection_duration both very short (10ms)\n- Do NOT create any streams\n- Wait for first timeout to fire\n- Verify:\n  - First timeout initiates drain correctly\n  - Stream list is empty, so connection closes immediately\n  - Second timeout does not cause double-close or state corruption\n  - Stats show proper transition (idle_timeout incremented, then close stats)\n  - For HTTP/1, soft drain flag is set correctly and codec doesn't receive goAway()\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nDrain logic is complex with multiple interlocking conditions. Bugs here could cause:\n- Graceful shutdowns to become abrupt (incomplete drains)\n- Connections to hang (drain never completes)\n- Double-close attempts (crashes or assertion failures)\n- Resource leaks in drain timer management\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Request Header Validation with Redirect and Transform Actions\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1200-1250 (validateHeaders path with header validation, transformation, redirect)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateHeaders()` function validates and transforms request headers. It handles multiple response codes:\n- HTTP 400 (BadRequest) for most failures\n- HTTP 501 (NotImplemented) for InvalidTransferEncoding\n- HTTP 307 (TemporaryRedirect) for path normalization redirects\n\nHowever, test coverage gaps include:\n- **Redirect responses with Location header** when `redirect=true && !is_grpc`\n- **GRPC-specific validation** failures (grpc_status set to Internal instead of response code)\n- **validateTrailers()** function (~1256-1300) which has similar structure but handles trailers validation with different codec-specific behavior for H/2 vs H/1 vs H/3\n- **Interaction with early_header_mutations** during validation failure\n- **ResponseCodeDetails tracking** when validation fails (must be set before sendLocalReply)\n\n**Proposed Test**: `RequestHeaderValidationWithRedirectAndGRPC`\n- Test case 1 (non-GRPC redirect):\n  - Send request with invalid path requiring normalization (e.g., double slashes)\n  - Verify: 307 response with Location header set to normalized path\n  - Stats show `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_` incremented\n  - ResponseCodeDetails set before response sent\n\n- Test case 2 (GRPC validation failure):\n  - Send GRPC request with invalid header underscore (H/2 protocol)\n  - Verify: Stream reset (not 400) per H/2 codec behavior\n  - ResponseCodeDetails set to appropriate UHV code\n  - Stats show `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_`\n\n- Test case 3 (trailers validation for H/1):\n  - Send HTTP/1 request with trailers\n  - Trailers contain invalid underscore in header name\n  - Verify: 400 BadRequest sent (not reset) per H/1 codec behavior\n  - Differs from H/2 reset behavior\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nHeader validation is first-line security. Bugs could cause:\n- Unsafe requests to bypass validation and reach upstream\n- Incorrect redirect responses leading to client loops\n- GRPC validation failures going undetected\n- Path traversal or injection attacks not blocked\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Filter Chain Iteration with Mixed Watermark States\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1625-1633 (handleDataIfStopAll), ~800-878 (decodeTrailers/encodeTrailers), ~880-933 (decodeMetadata)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe filter iteration logic handles three states for each filter:\n- `CanContinue` (no stop)\n- `StopSingleIteration` (stop this frame only, continue others)\n- `StopAllIteration` / `StopAllWatermark` (stop all frames until filter explicitly continues)\n\nThe code must handle:\n- Trailers added during data frames when filters have stopped\n- Metadata arriving after headers when chain is partially aborted\n- **Data arrival when filter is in StopAllWatermark state** → `handleDataIfStopAll()` must buffer data without continuing iteration\n- **Trailers during StopAllWatermark** → special handling in `decodeTrailers()` to skip stopped filters\n- **Metadata when decoder_filter_chain_aborted_** → must be saved and not discarded\n\nTests do not cover:\n- Trailers added by a filter while **previous filter is in StopAllWatermark state**\n- Metadata flowing through when **decoder_filter_chain_aborted_ is true** but filters haven't formally stopped\n- **Multiple metadata maps** arriving in sequence when chain is partially stopped\n- **Data + Trailers + Metadata order permutations** with StopAllWatermark filters\n\n**Proposed Test**: `FilterIterationTrailersWithStopAllWatermarkAndMetadata`\n- Setup 3 filters: F1 (decoder), F2 (decoder), F3 (terminal)\n- F1.decodeHeaders() → returns StopAllWatermark\n- Test harness calls F1.continueDecoding() with data and trailers together\n- Meanwhile F3 has generated and queued metadata for injection\n- Verify:\n  - F1 continues with both data and trailers\n  - Trailers properly delivered to F2 and F3\n  - Metadata queued during trailers processing is properly buffered\n  - No double-iteration of filters\n  - `iterate_from_current_filter_` flag correctly set to restart from F1\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nFilter state machine is complex and order-dependent. Bugs could cause:\n- Filters receiving data/trailers twice\n- Filters skipped entirely (data flows around them)\n- Deadlocks (filter waits for continuation that never comes)\n- Memory exhaustion (metadata/trailers stored but never processed)\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Recreation During Response Encoding with Complex State\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2461-2487 (recreateStream function with state transitions)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe `recreateStream()` function is called in rare cases (e.g., cache filter inject) to restart request processing on same connection. It:\n1. Sets `state_.is_internally_destroyed_ = true`\n2. Calls `doEndStream()` which resets the stream\n3. Creates a new stream and passes it back\n\nThis path is complex because:\n- The original stream's response_encoder is nulled to prevent double-reset notification\n- Deferred close check is disabled during recreation to allow new stream creation\n- Filter manager state must be properly reset between old and new stream\n- Response body encoding stops and switches to new stream context\n\nTest coverage gaps:\n- **Recreation when filters are in various stopped states** (StopAllIteration, etc.)\n- **Recreation with buffered trailers** from the original request\n- **Recreation with half-closed streams** (client sent end_stream, upstream hasn't)\n- **Stats and logging** around recreation (do stats reflect one stream or two?)\n- **Connection-level state** preservation (drain state, active stream list updates)\n- **Timeout state** - are stream timers properly cleaned up?\n\n**Proposed Test**: `RecreateStreamDuringFilterIterationWithTrailers`\n- Setup stream with request headers and trailers\n- Send headers → F1.decodeHeaders() returns StopAllIteration\n- Cache filter calls `encodeHeaders()` with modified request\n- Recreation triggered via `recreateStream()`\n- Verify:\n  - Original stream properly destroyed (state_.is_internally_destroyed_ = true)\n  - New stream created with same response_encoder\n  - Trailers from original request are not duplicated in new stream\n  - Filter timers (request_header_timer_, stream_idle_timeout) are reset\n  - Stream ID in stats reflects new stream, not old one\n  - `checkForDeferredClose()` is NOT called during recreation\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nRecreation is an internal implementation detail used by advanced filters. Bugs could cause:\n- Resource leaks (old stream never fully cleaned up)\n- Duplicate trailers/metadata in new stream\n- Timing attacks (old timers firing after new stream created)\n- Client confusion (stream reset notification + new response from same stream ID)\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\nThe analysis focused on:\n\n- **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc** - Connection lifecycle, codec management, stream creation, timeout handling, drain sequences\n- **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h** - Public interfaces and state machine definitions\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.cc** - Filter iteration logic, state transitions, metadata/data/trailers handling\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.h** - Filter chain execution interfaces\n- **source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc** - Header manipulation and validation\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc** - Primary test file (existing tests)\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc** - Secondary test file\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc** - Tertiary test file\n- **test/common/http/filter_manager_test.cc** - Filter manager unit tests\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h/cc** - Test infrastructure and mocks\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations for Test Implementation\n\n1. **Prioritize Gap 1 and Gap 2** (HIGH risk): These affect core connection/stream lifecycle\n2. **Use existing test infrastructure** in `conn_manager_impl_test_base.h` for mocks and setup\n3. **Leverage InSequence** for strict ordering verification of codec/stream operations\n4. **Create reusable test fixtures** for common scenarios (N streams in various states, timeout sequences)\n5. **Add mutation testing** to catch subtle state bugs (e.g., forgot to set response_flag)\n6. **Monitor stats assertions** - many bugs manifest as incorrect stat increments\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Analysis of `conn_manager_impl.cc`, `filter_manager.cc`, and `header_map_impl.cc` reveals **5 significant untested code paths** that could allow bugs in connection management, error handling, metadata processing, and filter state transitions to slip through. These gaps primarily affect error scenarios, edge cases in filter iteration, and complex state transitions that are difficult to trigger in normal operation.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Codec Error Handling Under Connection State Changes\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~463-482 (handleCodecErrorImpl, handleCodecError, handleCodecOverloadError)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Description**:\nThe functions `handleCodecError()`, `handleCodecErrorImpl()`, and `handleCodecOverloadError()` are responsible for terminating the connection when the codec encounters protocol errors or overload conditions. These functions are called from `onData()` after codec dispatch fails. However, the test suite lacks comprehensive coverage for:\n- Codec errors that occur when there are **active streams with various states** (some completed, some in-progress, some in filter chain)\n- The interaction between `handleCodecError()` and deferred deletion of streams\n- Proper cleanup when codec errors occur during H/1 vs H/2 vs H/3 protocols\n- The `handleCodecOverloadError()` path which sets `OverloadManager` response flag instead of protocol error flag\n\n**Proposed Test**: `CodecErrorWithActiveStreamsInFilterChain`\n- Create multiple concurrent streams in different states:\n  - Stream 1: stuck in decoder filter (StopAllIteration)\n  - Stream 2: waiting for upstream response\n  - Stream 3: about to encode response\n- Inject a codec error via mock codec\n- Verify:\n  - All active streams are reset with proper response flags\n  - Response flag is set correctly (DownstreamProtocolError vs OverloadManager)\n  - Connection is properly closed without leaks\n  - Stream details in logs reflect the error state\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nCodec errors are rare but catastrophic. If stream cleanup is incorrect, it could lead to:\n- Resource leaks (streams not deleted from streams_ list)\n- Incorrect stats increments (double-counting, missing counters)\n- Filters accessing invalid stream state after closure\n- Clients not receiving reset notifications\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Connection Drain Sequence Edge Cases\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~756-794 (onIdleTimeout, onConnectionDurationTimeout, onDrainTimeout, startDrainSequence)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Description**:\nThe drain sequence is initiated when timeouts occur or when connection should enter graceful shutdown. The code paths handle:\n- Idle timeout with active streams → start drain\n- Max connection duration reached with/without HTTP/1 safe mode\n- Drain timeout transition from NotDraining → Closing\n\nHowever, tests do not cover:\n- **Drain sequence when connection has NO streams** (idle_timeout fires but streams_ is empty) → should immediately close\n- **Simultaneous timeout signals** (both idle_timeout and connection_duration_timer_ fire in quick succession)\n- **HTTP/1 soft drain** path where `soft_drain_http1_` is set and `codec_->goAway()` must not be called\n- **Drain state transitions** when streams finish during drain sequence\n- **checkForDeferredClose() interaction** with drain timeouts\n\n**Proposed Test**: `DrainSequenceWithNoStreamsAndQuickTimer`\n- Setup connection with idle_timeout and max_connection_duration both very short (10ms)\n- Do NOT create any streams\n- Wait for first timeout to fire\n- Verify:\n  - First timeout initiates drain correctly\n  - Stream list is empty, so connection closes immediately\n  - Second timeout does not cause double-close or state corruption\n  - Stats show proper transition (idle_timeout incremented, then close stats)\n  - For HTTP/1, soft drain flag is set correctly and codec doesn't receive goAway()\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nDrain logic is complex with multiple interlocking conditions. Bugs here could cause:\n- Graceful shutdowns to become abrupt (incomplete drains)\n- Connections to hang (drain never completes)\n- Double-close attempts (crashes or assertion failures)\n- Resource leaks in drain timer management\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Request Header Validation with Redirect and Transform Actions\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1200-1250 (validateHeaders path with header validation, transformation, redirect)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateHeaders()` function validates and transforms request headers. It handles multiple response codes:\n- HTTP 400 (BadRequest) for most failures\n- HTTP 501 (NotImplemented) for InvalidTransferEncoding\n- HTTP 307 (TemporaryRedirect) for path normalization redirects\n\nHowever, test coverage gaps include:\n- **Redirect responses with Location header** when `redirect=true && !is_grpc`\n- **GRPC-specific validation** failures (grpc_status set to Internal instead of response code)\n- **validateTrailers()** function (~1256-1300) which has similar structure but handles trailers validation with different codec-specific behavior for H/2 vs H/1 vs H/3\n- **Interaction with early_header_mutations** during validation failure\n- **ResponseCodeDetails tracking** when validation fails (must be set before sendLocalReply)\n\n**Proposed Test**: `RequestHeaderValidationWithRedirectAndGRPC`\n- Test case 1 (non-GRPC redirect):\n  - Send request with invalid path requiring normalization (e.g., double slashes)\n  - Verify: 307 response with Location header set to normalized path\n  - Stats show `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_` incremented\n  - ResponseCodeDetails set before response sent\n\n- Test case 2 (GRPC validation failure):\n  - Send GRPC request with invalid header underscore (H/2 protocol)\n  - Verify: Stream reset (not 400) per H/2 codec behavior\n  - ResponseCodeDetails set to appropriate UHV code\n  - Stats show `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_`\n\n- Test case 3 (trailers validation for H/1):\n  - Send HTTP/1 request with trailers\n  - Trailers contain invalid underscore in header name\n  - Verify: 400 BadRequest sent (not reset) per H/1 codec behavior\n  - Differs from H/2 reset behavior\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nHeader validation is first-line security. Bugs could cause:\n- Unsafe requests to bypass validation and reach upstream\n- Incorrect redirect responses leading to client loops\n- GRPC validation failures going undetected\n- Path traversal or injection attacks not blocked\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Filter Chain Iteration with Mixed Watermark States\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1625-1633 (handleDataIfStopAll), ~800-878 (decodeTrailers/encodeTrailers), ~880-933 (decodeMetadata)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe filter iteration logic handles three states for each filter:\n- `CanContinue` (no stop)\n- `StopSingleIteration` (stop this frame only, continue others)\n- `StopAllIteration` / `StopAllWatermark` (stop all frames until filter explicitly continues)\n\nThe code must handle:\n- Trailers added during data frames when filters have stopped\n- Metadata arriving after headers when chain is partially aborted\n- **Data arrival when filter is in StopAllWatermark state** → `handleDataIfStopAll()` must buffer data without continuing iteration\n- **Trailers during StopAllWatermark** → special handling in `decodeTrailers()` to skip stopped filters\n- **Metadata when decoder_filter_chain_aborted_** → must be saved and not discarded\n\nTests do not cover:\n- Trailers added by a filter while **previous filter is in StopAllWatermark state**\n- Metadata flowing through when **decoder_filter_chain_aborted_ is true** but filters haven't formally stopped\n- **Multiple metadata maps** arriving in sequence when chain is partially stopped\n- **Data + Trailers + Metadata order permutations** with StopAllWatermark filters\n\n**Proposed Test**: `FilterIterationTrailersWithStopAllWatermarkAndMetadata`\n- Setup 3 filters: F1 (decoder), F2 (decoder), F3 (terminal)\n- F1.decodeHeaders() → returns StopAllWatermark\n- Test harness calls F1.continueDecoding() with data and trailers together\n- Meanwhile F3 has generated and queued metadata for injection\n- Verify:\n  - F1 continues with both data and trailers\n  - Trailers properly delivered to F2 and F3\n  - Metadata queued during trailers processing is properly buffered\n  - No double-iteration of filters\n  - `iterate_from_current_filter_` flag correctly set to restart from F1\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nFilter state machine is complex and order-dependent. Bugs could cause:\n- Filters receiving data/trailers twice\n- Filters skipped entirely (data flows around them)\n- Deadlocks (filter waits for continuation that never comes)\n- Memory exhaustion (metadata/trailers stored but never processed)\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Recreation During Response Encoding with Complex State\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2461-2487 (recreateStream function with state transitions)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Description**:\nThe `recreateStream()` function is called in rare cases (e.g., cache filter inject) to restart request processing on same connection. It:\n1. Sets `state_.is_internally_destroyed_ = true`\n2. Calls `doEndStream()` which resets the stream\n3. Creates a new stream and passes it back\n\nThis path is complex because:\n- The original stream's response_encoder is nulled to prevent double-reset notification\n- Deferred close check is disabled during recreation to allow new stream creation\n- Filter manager state must be properly reset between old and new stream\n- Response body encoding stops and switches to new stream context\n\nTest coverage gaps:\n- **Recreation when filters are in various stopped states** (StopAllIteration, etc.)\n- **Recreation with buffered trailers** from the original request\n- **Recreation with half-closed streams** (client sent end_stream, upstream hasn't)\n- **Stats and logging** around recreation (do stats reflect one stream or two?)\n- **Connection-level state** preservation (drain state, active stream list updates)\n- **Timeout state** - are stream timers properly cleaned up?\n\n**Proposed Test**: `RecreateStreamDuringFilterIterationWithTrailers`\n- Setup stream with request headers and trailers\n- Send headers → F1.decodeHeaders() returns StopAllIteration\n- Cache filter calls `encodeHeaders()` with modified request\n- Recreation triggered via `recreateStream()`\n- Verify:\n  - Original stream properly destroyed (state_.is_internally_destroyed_ = true)\n  - New stream created with same response_encoder\n  - Trailers from original request are not duplicated in new stream\n  - Filter timers (request_header_timer_, stream_idle_timeout) are reset\n  - Stream ID in stats reflects new stream, not old one\n  - `checkForDeferredClose()` is NOT called during recreation\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nRecreation is an internal implementation detail used by advanced filters. Bugs could cause:\n- Resource leaks (old stream never fully cleaned up)\n- Duplicate trailers/metadata in new stream\n- Timing attacks (old timers firing after new stream created)\n- Client confusion (stream reset notification + new response from same stream ID)\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\nThe analysis focused on:\n\n- **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc** - Connection lifecycle, codec management, stream creation, timeout handling, drain sequences\n- **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h** - Public interfaces and state machine definitions\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.cc** - Filter iteration logic, state transitions, metadata/data/trailers handling\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.h** - Filter chain execution interfaces\n- **source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc** - Header manipulation and validation\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc** - Primary test file (existing tests)\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc** - Secondary test file\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc** - Tertiary test file\n- **test/common/http/filter_manager_test.cc** - Filter manager unit tests\n- **test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h/cc** - Test infrastructure and mocks\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations for Test Implementation\n\n1. **Prioritize Gap 1 and Gap 2** (HIGH risk): These affect core connection/stream lifecycle\n2. **Use existing test infrastructure** in `conn_manager_impl_test_base.h` for mocks and setup\n3. **Leverage InSequence** for strict ordering verification of codec/stream operations\n4. **Create reusable test fixtures** for common scenarios (N streams in various states, timeout sequences)\n5. **Add mutation testing** to catch subtle state bugs (e.g., forgot to set response_flag)\n6. **Monitor stats assertions** - many bugs manifest as incorrect stat increments\n\n","numLines":251,"startLine":1,"totalLines":251}}}
